<Rate>5<//Rate>< text>
(Translated by Google) Located in the center of LAX, the theme building that symbolizes LAX.
It used to be a restaurant, but now it's closed.

You can go up to the observation deck on the top floor from 9am to 5pm for only two days, Saturday and Sunday, the second weekend of every month. (Currently, the observation deck is also closed.)

The four arch pillars extend north, south, east and west.

<Review>(Translated by Google) The theme building at the airport attracts attention by its futuristic appearance. Built in 1961, it is quite appropriate at the time. The great powers raised claims to space, while at the same time rumors about UFOs, that is, flying objects with living things from other planets, which some people believed, no matter how crazy this idea was. Frequently, these supposed objects were described and illustrated with a disk-shaped form.
The architect of this building planned the UFO-like design to a huge extent, which was to unite all terminal buildings and parking garages under a huge glass dome. The intended size was rejected, but they wanted to appreciate the fascination that embodied the design, and agreed to a strongly redimensionierten construction. The opinions expressed at the time oscillated between a flying saucer and a huge white spider.
After the opening, the influx of curious people was enormous, as you had a fascinating view of the aircraft from the viewing platform.
After 9/11, the attacks in New York, then came immediately security concerns, the restaurant was there, which was closed. Today, the building is basically no longer accessible to the public. Nevertheless, the distinctive building remains a symbol of the space age, which is often used as a photo subject.

< text>
This location is stunning! Floor to ceiling windows, lively atmosphere, cute decor, and great branding. The service was on point and very friendly. It‚Äôs been a long time since I had a server tell me their name and offer to tell me about the menu.

Menu consists of traditional and non traditional dishes. I would guess the most popular are the hummus bowls which are a bowl of hummus with toppings. Overall the food was ok. I would say pretty typical but served in a more trendy way. The pita bread was unique. Quite a bit more puffy then normal. It would be nice if the pita was fresh (crispy outside, and soft inside), instead of just kept in a warmer tray all day.

They have a take out section that didn‚Äôt have anyone working. The rest of the restaurant is all sit down. Not the typical order at the counter Mediterranean fare. I‚Äôll be back to try again and enjoy the great atmosphere.< /text>

<user_name>Toshinobu Kubota< /user_name><date>1553485784732< /date>< rate>
5</rate>
< Text>
Oren's Hummus is a fairly new addition to the Cupertino Main Street shopping plaza, and it is definitely a welcome sight. There are plenty of Chinese dining options in the area due to the city it's located in, but Oren's provides a depth to the dining choices in this hip new plaza. My must orders are; Hummus Sabich (great fried eggplant with creamy Hummus all wrapped in a warm and fluffy pita bread), chicken rice bowl (the rice has great flavors and the chicken is tender with great spices), beef kebab (great spices again and it comes with two dips or sides), and sweet potato fries (comes out piping hot with red pepper mayo).
After chowing down on this big meal, I walked out feeling healthy and not weighed down with all the grease found in other restaurants. Oren's provide a fresh alternative to eat healthy while enjoying good ingredients prepared well. I would definitely return to enjoy another "healthy-decision" meal.</Text>

<rate>3</rate>< review>
The hummus here is really good. I ordered chicken skewers with falafel and hummus side with pita bread. The bread here is super fluffy and tastes amazing with the hummus. The chicken is tender and juicy. Falafel is pretty decent too. Tried some of my friend's fried cauliflower and it was also not bad. Her eggplant sauce side left us kind of confused. It didn't taste bad, but it also tasted like the smell of a leather car. You'd think that's a bad thing, but we were just conflicted on what we thought of it. Anyway, the only reason she got that instead of a side of hummus is because she doesn't really like hummus. I love hummus though so I'd definitely recommend it. It is called Oren's hummus for a reason.< /review>

Wine is 50% off on Wednesdays (glass and bottle)!! Service is always attentive, and food is the best and consistent every time. I love all the dips, but especially Oren's Eggplant, Greek-style Eggplant, Labne, marinated beet, and of course the hummus topped with lamb or beef (I have yet to try the chicken liver).
